CITY OF SAN MATEO
City Council Regular Meeting
May 18, 2020
7:00 PM
COUNCIL MEMBERS
Joe Goethals, Mayor
Eric Rodriguez, Deputy Mayor
Rick Bonilla
Amourence Lee
Diane Papan
AGENDA
DUE TO THE STATE OF CALIFORNIA’S DECLARATION OF EMERGENCY – THIS MEETING IS BEING HELD
PURSUANT TO AUTHORIZATION FROM GOVERNOR NEWSOM’S EXECUTIVE ORDERS –
CITY COUNCIL AND COMMISSION MEETINGS ARE NO LONGER OPEN TO IN-PERSON ATTENDANCE.
ANYONE CAN WATCH AND PROVIDE COMMENTS REMOTELY IN THE WAYS
DESCRIBED AT THE END OF THE AGENDA.
To join via Zoom – click here: May 18, 2020 Zoom Meeting
To join via telephone: (408) 638-0968
Enter Conference ID: 892 0985 5085
CALL TO ORDER
Pledge of Allegiance
Roll Call
CONSENT CALENDAR
All matters listed under the Consent Calendar are considered by the Council to be routine and will be enacted by one motion without
discussion. If discussion is desired, that item may be removed and considered separately.
1.
City Council Meeting Minutes – Approval
Approve the minutes of the City Council Special and Regular meeting of May 4, 2020 and the Special Meeting of
May 11, 2020.
2.
Merit Employees Salary Schedule – Approval
Adopt a Resolution to authorize and approve the City of San Mateo merit employee current pay rates and ranges
(salary schedule).
3.
Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements – Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 10 to Stantec Consulting Services, Inc. to provide engineering services during
construction for the Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements project’s Underground Flow Equalization
System package in an amount not to exceed $1,290,500, for a total agreement amount of $15,600,841; increase
the contingency reserve by $129,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in
substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
1 of 328

--- page 2 ---
4.
Community Development Block Grant 2020-21 Annual Action Plan – Adoption; and Community Participation Plan
and 2018-2022 Consolidated Plan – Amendments
Adopt the 2020-21 Annual Action Plan for the Community Development Block Grant and HOME programs, and
adopt amendments to the Community Participation Plan and the 2018-22 Consolidated Plan.
5.
Emergency Rental Assistance – Agreement
Approve an agreement with Samaritan House to provide rental assistance payments to income eligible residents
in the amount of $440,000 and authorize City Manager to execute the agreement in substantially the form
presented.
6.
Animal Control and Licensing Services - Amendment
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with the County of San Mateo for continued facilitation and
coordination of Animal Control and Licensing Services for an additional one-year term beginning July 1, 2020, and
authorize the City Manager to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented.
7.
AXON Body Worn Camera and Taser Officer Safety Plan Bundle – Agreement
Adopt a Resolution to use an alternative purchasing method to approve an agreement with Axon Enterprise, Inc.,
for an Officer Safety Plan bundle contract for Police Department Body Worn Cameras and Conducted Energy
Devices (Tasers) in the total amount of $1,267,301.58 for a five-year term, with an option to renew for an
additional five-year term in 2025; and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreement in substantially the
form presented.
PUBLIC COMMENT
Members of the public wishing to comment on any item not appearing on the agenda may address the City Council at this time. State
law prevents Council from taking action on any matter not on the agenda; your comments may be referred to staff for follow up.
Public comment is limited to a total of 15 minutes; however, an opportunity for additional public comment may be provided later in
the agenda.
OLD BUSINESS
8.
Emergency Ordinance – Extending a Moratorium on Small Business Evictions Related to Covid-19
Adopt an Emergency Ordinance to amend the Emergency Moratorium on Small Business Evictions Caused by
COVID-19 to Extend the Term of the Moratorium and the Time for Repayment of Deferred Rent.
9.
Covid 19 Update (#9)
Receive update on operational impacts and other City efforts related to COVID-19 and confirm rules and
regulations issued by the City Manager acting as the Director of Emergency Services in response to declared
emergency.
NEW BUSINESS
10.
Metrics for Local Transportation Analysis for New Development – Use of Level of Service and Vehicle Miles
Traveled
Receive an informational report on metrics for local transportation analysis, provide direction to staff on future
amendments to the current General Plan, and consider approval of staff’s recommendations regarding vehicle
miles traveled analysis.
11.
Ballot Measure Council Ad Hoc Subcommittee – Recommendation
Oppose the initiative measure extending Measure P height limits for 10 years.

--- page 3 ---
12.
November 3, 2020 General Municipal Election – Calling the Election and Placing a Measure on the Ballot
Adopt a Resolution to call for and conduct the November 3, 2020 General Municipal Election; request
consolidation with San Mateo County for election services and authorize the City Clerk to execute the Service
Agreement for the Provision of Election Services with the County of San Mateo; and adopt a Resolution to place
the measure to Extend Measure P on the ballot.
REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
City Manager, City Attorney and Council Members report on their various assignments and liaison roles and Council requests for
scheduling future items.
ADJOURNMENT
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
AGENDAS: Agendas and material are posted on the City’s website on the Friday preceding each Council Meeting and can be viewed
on the City's website at www.cityofsanmateo.org . Any supplemental material distributed to the Council after the posting of the agenda
will be made part of the official record.
WATCHING A MEETING ON TV: City Council meetings are broadcast live on
Comcast/channel 27, Wave/channel 26, or AT&T/channel 99.
For transmission problems during the broadcast, please call (650) 522-7099.
For all other broadcast comments, call (650) 522-7040, Monday-Friday, 8 a.m. - 5 p.m.
WATCHING A MEETING ON A COMPUTER: There are three ways to stream.
1) Public Meeting Portal www.cityofsanmateo.org/publicmeetings
2) City YouTube channel and stream it on YouTube: http://youtube.com/CityofSanMateo
3) Watch TV live stream: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/193/Channel-San-Mateo-Live-Stream
PUBLIC COMMENTS – Can be received in the following ways (Time limits will apply) :
Prior to the meeting in writing: Send comments to: clerk@cityofsanmateo.org until 4 p.m. the day of the meeting.
During the meeting by computer: Click the link at the top of the agenda and you’ll be added to the meeting. All attendees are muted
by default. To speak press the “Raise Your Hand” icon and you will be called on at the appropriate time.
During the meeting by telephone: Call (408) 638-0968 and enter the conference ID found at the top of the meeting agenda. To
indicate you want to provide public comment, press *9 to raise your hand.
When called upon, state your name and provide your comments.
ACCESSIBILITY: In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act, those with disabilities requiring special accommodations to
participate in this meeting may contact the City Clerk’s Office at (650) 522-7040 or clerk@cityofsanmateo.org. Notification 48 hours
prior to the meeting will enable the City to make reasonable arrangements to ensure accessibility to this meeting.

CALL TO ORDER This meeting is being held under the provisions of State of California Governor Gavin Newsom’s 
Executive Order N-29-20; in which Brown Act regulations are relaxed to allow members to remote in due to the

CONSENT CALENDAR 
The following items, 1 through 8, were considered to be routine by the City Council. Items 9 and 10 were removed to be 
considered separately. After the titles of the items were read by the City Clerk, the public was invited to comment and 
there were no speakers. Motion passed 5-0.
Moved:
Bonilla, Seconded: Papan
Ayes: 
Goethals, Rodriguez, Bonilla, Papan and Lee
Noes: 
None
1.
City Council Meeting Minutes - Approval
Approve the minutes of the City Council's regular and special meeting of of April 20, 2020 and the special meeting of 
April 27, 2020.
 
2.
Disposition of the Property Jointly Owned by the City Attorney and the City of San Mateo
Direct the City Attorney to proceed with the sale of the property jointly owned by the City Attorney and the City of 
San Mateo to a third party, with the proceeds being split between the City Attorney and the City of San Mateo based 
on the original agreement, as modified as requested by the City Attorney.
 
3.
Seamless Bay Area - Integrated Public Transit Support 
Adopt a Resolution to support Seamless Bay Area’s “Seamless Transit Principles” which commits to working 
collaboratively with other agencies to develop a highly integrated regional transportation system. 
Enactment:  Resolution No. 41 (2020)
 
4.
City-Owned Poles ExteNet Systems - Master License Agreement 
Approve a Master License Agreement with ExteNet Systems, LLC to allow small cell installations on City owned poles.
 
5.
Public Works Backhoe Purchase – Contract
Adopt a Resolution to approve an alternative purchasing to approve a contract with Sonsray Machinery for the

Approve a professional services agreement with Terraphase Engineering, Inc. for construction monitoring support 
services for the Clean Water Program’s Wastewater Treatment Plant Upgrade and Expansion Project and

Improvement project in the amount of $2,693,541, establish a contingency reserve of $270,000, and authorize the 
Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue amendments within 
the contingency reserve.
 
END OF CONSENT CALENDAR
REMOVED FROM CONSENT CALENDAR
Items 9 and 10 were considered together in one vote. These items were removed by Council Member Bonilla to 
comment on his concern that the bidding process was irregular and lacking in transparency. He requested a 
prevailing wage monitor on these projects. Council concurred with the request. Council asked questions of staff.

PUBLIC COMMENT
There were no speakers.
OLD BUSINESS
 
11. COVID-19 Update (#7)
City Manager Drew Corbett provided an update on operational impacts and other City efforts related to COVID-19 
and requested Council confirm the rules and regulations issued by the City Manager acting as the Director of 
Emergency Services in response to the declared emergency. Council asked questions of staff. Public Comment – 
There were no speakers. Council confirmed the adjustments to operations, deployment of personnel, cancellation of 
summer events, and special leave for emergency responders. Council concurred in the recommendation to defer 
June rents to private tenants of City-owned properties and to extend the rent commencement date for Rise Pizza by 
two months. Motion passed 5-0. 
Moved:
Bonilla, Seconded: Papan
Ayes: 
Goethals, Rodriguez, Papan, Bonilla, and Lee
Noes: 
None
 
12. Calling Election on Ballot Measure relating to the Extension of Measure P Policies
City Attorney Shawn Mason provided a report and requested direction on scheduling at a future meeting the action 
to call the regular election on the qualified ballot measure. Council asked questions of staff. Public Comment – Alex 
Melendrez, Housing Leadership Council, commented on the need to place this on the ballot although he is not in 
favor of it. Stewart Hyland, Housing Leadership Council, stated he supported putting this on the ballot. Motion 
passed 5-0 to put this item on the next meeting on May 18, 2020 for action.
Moved:
Bonilla, Seconded: Rodriguez
Ayes: 
Goethals, Rodriguez, Papan, Bonilla, and Lee
Noes: 
None
Discussion ensued on if the Legislative Committee should meet and take a position on the ballot measure. Upon 
clarification of the Legislative Committee’s mission in the Council Guidelines it was decided that Mayor Goethals and 
Deputy Mayor Rodriguez would form a sub-committee to make a recommendation to Council on a position to take 
on the ballot measure. Council also directed staff to look into closing down specific streets to allow for street dining 
when restaurants are allowed to reopen to encourage healthy and safe social distancing and support the businesses.
REPORTS AND ANNOUNCEMENTS
The City Manager, City Attorney, and Council Members reported on their various assignments and liaison roles. Council 
gave a shout out to staff for their great work during this difficult time.
ADJOURNMENT
The meeting adjourned at 8:05 p.m.

CITY OF SAN MATEO

Monday, May 11, 2020
Remote 6:15 PM
Special Meeting
 
This meeting is being held under the provisions of State of California Governor Gavin Newsom’s Executive Order N-29-20; 
in which Brown Act regulations are relaxed to allow members to remote in due to the Coronavirus Covid-19 health 
emergency. 
CALL TO ORDER
 
Pledge of Allegiance 
Roll Call
Remote:    Mayor Goethals, Deputy Mayor Rodriguez, Council Members: Bonilla, Papan and Lee 
OLD BUSINESS
1.
Emergency Ordinance – Imposing a Moratorium on Small Business Evictions Related to COVID-19
City Attorney Shawn Mason reported on activities taken to date and information on extending the emergency 
ordinance, currently sunsetting on 5/31/2020, to impose a moratorium on evictions for nonpayment of rent by 
small business tenants impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic. Council asked questions of staff. Public Comment – 
there were no speakers. Council by consensus directed the City Attorney to place this item for adoption on the 
5/18/2020 agenda extending the expiration to 6/30/2020 and to provide some consideration for extension of 
time for payback of back rent, which is currently set at six months.
2.
COVID-19 Update (#8)
City Manager Drew Corbett update on operational impacts and other City efforts related to COVID-19. Council 
asked questions of staff. Public Comment – Adam Loraine commented with appreciation for the City’s efforts. 
Discussion ensued among Council on ensuring small businesses, in addition to restaurants, that all business needs 
are understood. Council members who attend the County briefing call will ask the County to look into a regional 
response to third party food delivery charges. 
NEW BUSINESS
3.
Fiscal Sustainability Plan - Direction
Finance Director Rich Lee provided options on the path forward with regard to the City's Fiscal Sustainability Plan. 
He outlined short-term (2021 only) and long-term strategies (10-year term) to address the expected $7.8 million 
shortfall in the 2020-21 budget and reviewed long term impacts on the General Fund’s Five-Year Forecast due to 
the economic issues from COVID-19. He outlined the different approaches being considered from modifications 
to operations, employee compensation, funding support, and revenue enhancement. He noted the focus was on 
minimal impact to service levels. Council asked questions of staff. Public Comment – Adam Loraine supported the 
staff recommendation. Council provided comments and supported the four-pronged staff recommendation. City 
Manager Drew Corbett noted that the recommendations for tonight are for the 2020-21 Budget and that staff is 
planning on coming back in October 2020 with longer term opportunities. 
10 of 328

--- page 11 ---
City Council Special Meeting Minutes – 05/11/2020
Page 2
Approve the Fiscal Sustainability Plan with four elements: negotiate employee compensation restructuring; 
strategic elimination of positions; limit Capital Improvement Program support; and revenue enhancement 
through Transient Occupancy Tax measure or possible furloughs the week between Christmas and New Year’s. 
Motion Passed 5-0.
Moved:
Goethals, Seconded: Bonilla
Ayes: 
Goethals, Rodriguez, Bonilla, Papan and Lee
Noes: 
None
ADJOURNMENT 
The Meeting adjourned at 8:15 pm.
APPROVED BY:

City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Human Resources Department
MEETING DATE:
May 18, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Merit Employees Salary Schedule – Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to authorize and approve the City of San Mateo merit employee current pay rates and ranges (salary 
schedule).
BACKGROUND:
Pursuant to Municipal Code Section 4.02, the City Council provides for the compensation of all officers and employees and 
salaries shall be fixed by Resolution. Title 2 of the California Code of Regulations (CCR), Section 570.5, requires the City 
Council to adopt a full salary schedule as a standalone document detailing the rates of pay for each City classification, and 
to maintain this salary schedule as a publicly available document for at least five years. The California Public Employees’ 
Retirement System (CALPERS) uses this salary schedule to determine the “compensation earnable” when calculating the 
monthly pension an individual will receive when they retire. “Compensation earnable” is defined by the Public Employees’ 
Retirement Law (PERL) Government Code Sections 20636 and 20636.1 as pay rate and special compensation as defined in 
the statutes. The City of San Mateo’s salary schedule is consistent with the existing classifications and pay rates for current 
employees at this time, and no changes to the various salary ranges are proposed by the adoption of this salary schedule. 
The City Manager, City Attorney, Department Heads, Deputy Directors and Merit Employees Salary Schedule (Exhibit A) 
reflects salary changes previously approved by the Council in Resolutions. Salary schedules are available to the public on 
the City’s website. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no fiscal impact related to the adoption of this Resolution. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This item is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not result in 
direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 - Proposed Resolution 
Exhibit A - Salary Schedule 
STAFF CONTACT
Casey Echarte, Director of Human Resources

CITY OF SAN MATEO 
RESOLUTION NO. __ (2020) 
 
ADOPTING THE CITY OF SAN MATEO PAYRATES AND RANGES  
(SALARY SCHEDULE) 
 
WHEREAS, pursuant to Municipal Code Section 4.02, the City Council provides for the compensation of 
all officers and employees and salaries shall be fixed by resolution; and 
 
WHEREAS, Title 2 of the California Code of Regulations (CCR), Section 570.5, requires the City Council 
to adopt a full salary schedule, as a standalone document detailing the rates of pay for each City classification; 
and 
 
WHEREAS, the City must maintain salary schedules as publicly available documents for at least five 
years; and 
 
WHEREAS, the California Public Employees’ Retirement System (CALPERS) uses the salary schedules to 
determine “compensation earnable”; and 
 
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo Salary Schedule is consistent with the existing classifications and pay 
rates for current employees at this time and no changes to the various salary ranges are proposed by the 
adoption of the salary schedule; and 
 
WHEREAS, this salary schedule reflects salary changes previously approved by the Council in 
Resolutions; and 
 
WHEREAS, no appropriation of additional funds is necessary; 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, 
HEREBY RESOLVES that: 
 
1. The pay rates and ranges set forth in the Salary Schedule attached as Exhibit A is approved.

PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
May 18, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements – Amendment 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 10 to Stantec Consulting Services, Inc. to provide engineering services during construction for 
the Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements project’s Underground Flow Equalization System package in an 
amount not to exceed $1,290,500, for a total agreement amount of $15,600,841; increase the contingency reserve by 
$129,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the amendment in substantially the form presented and 
issue change orders within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Clean Water Program includes improvements to the City’s sanitary sewer collection system to prevent sanitary sewer 
overflows and unauthorized discharges. The Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements (Basins 2 and 3) project 
increases capacity and improves flow management for wet weather flows. Basins 2 and 3 has various construction 
packages that include improvements to pump stations, sewers, and the Underground Flow Equalization System (UFES). 
The UFES consists of a concrete 5.3 million gallon underground wastewater holding structure, pump station, diversion 
sewers and force main, odor control equipment room, and an aboveground electrical building. The UFES project was 
advertised for construction in January 2020 and is currently scheduled to start construction activities in Summer 2020. 
Stantec Consulting Services, Inc. (Stantec) was selected as the design consultant for the Basins 2 and 3 project and 
completed the design for the UFES construction package. Amendment No. 10 specifically requests budget and scope 
associated with the UFES package for Stantec to provide engineering services during construction, which includes reviews 
of submittals and requests for information, site visits, construction meeting support, construction monitoring support, 
change order reviews, start-up and commission. 
Stantec submitted an initial proposal to provide engineering services during construction. Staff reviewed and negotiated 
the scope and fee to a level that is reasonable for the scope of work and expertise required. Staff recommends approving 
Amendment No. 10 to Stantec with a not-to-exceed amount of $1,290,500 and an increase of $129,000 to the contingency 
reserve to address unknown risks or changes needed to complete the work. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The initial authorized contract agreement with Stantec was in the amount of $1,742,000. The prior approved amendments 
are in the table shown below. Amendment No. 10 increases the contract amount by $1,290,500, bringing the total 
contract amount to $15,600,841 for all of Basins 2 and 3. Amendment No. 10 also increases the contingency amount by 
$129,000 for a total contingency amount of $322,000. Funding for Amendment No. 10 is available in Project 46S003 - 
Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements.

This project is subject to the requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), the general components of 
which are included as part of the Final Environmental Impact Report (Final EIR) (SCH No. 2018092013) that was prepared

engineering design services contract will not have a significant effect on the environment.

WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo (“City”), a municipal corporation of the State of California, and 
Stantec Consulting Services Inc. (“CONSULTANT”), entered into an Agreement for Basins 2 and 3 
Collection System Improvements Project No. 46S003 (“Agreement”) on April 26, 2016; and 
 
 
WHEREAS, City and CONSULTANT wish to amend the Agreement to extend the completion date 
and add scope of this Agreement. 
 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, the parties agree as follows: 
 
1. 
Section 1 – Scope of Project of the Agreement is amended to reference “Exhibits A, A1, 
A2, A3, A4, A5, A6, A7, A8, A9 and A10”. Exhibit A10 to the Agreement is attached and 
incorporated by reference.  
 
2. 
Section 7 – Term, Progress and Completion of the Agreement is amended to reference 
“Exhibits B, B1, B2, B3, B4, B5, B6 and B7”. Exhibit B7 to the Agreement is attached and 
incorporated by reference. 
 
3. 
Section 8 – Payment of the Agreement is amended to state “City agrees to pay 
CONSULTANT a fee based on verified time and materials not to exceed $15,600,841. 
Requests for payments shall be itemized and correspond to the various items of work 
described in Exhibits A1, A2, A3, A4, A5, A6, A7, A8, A9 and A10 and shall be based on 
the rate and cost schedule set forth in Exhibits C1, C2, C3, C4, C5, C6 and C7.” Exhibit C7 
to the Agreement is attached and incorporated by reference. 
 
4. 
The remaining terms of the Agreement remain in full force and effect.

SCOPE OF SERVICES 
The Consultant will provide engineering services for all Project Elements listed in this Scope of Services. 
The project, and fee negotiations, is being executed in three phases. This Basins 2 and 3 Collection 
System Improvements project scope currently describes Phase 3, Engineering Services During 
Construction (ESDC), for the Underground Flow Equalization System (UFES) construction package. 
Phase 3 (Current Authorization) 
• 
Task 1 – General Services 
• 
Task 7 – Construction Phase Services 
• 
Task 8 – Construction Monitoring 
Tasks that are required of the Consultant under these categories are detailed in the following sections. 
Throughout the construction of this project, the Consultant will submit deliverables for review and 
approval by the City and other governing agencies as required. A listing of deliverables is provided in this 
Scope of Services. 
The City reserves the right to discontinue, alter, or postpone services at any time. 
Overall Scope Assumptions:  Phase 2 of the Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements project is 
ongoing and tasks in this scope of work will only be modified to incorporate Phase 3 services.  
TASK 1 – GENERAL SERVICES 
General Services include tasks that will be performed by the Consultant throughout the project.  These 
services include:   
• 
Project Management 
• 
Management of Subconsultants 
Task 1.1 – Project Management 
Task 1.1.1 – General Management 
Because the construction of this project will be beyond the design tasks, Consultant assumed project 
management is estimated for the ESDC support.   
Task 1.1.4 and 1.1.5 – Progress Reports and Invoices 
The Consultant will prepare and submit monthly progress reports including the engineering services 
during construction.  These reports will be included with the monthly invoice.   
Task 1.1.7 – Progress Schedule 
Includes monthly updates of the schedule. 
Task 1.5 – Management of Subconsultants 
If the Consultant requires the services of any Subconsultants, explain why they are needed, and provide 
a general description of their effort.  The Consultant will manage the activities of Subconsultants during 
performance of the project. 
52 of 328

--- page 53 ---
Page 3 of 22 
 
 
Task 1.5 Assumptions: 
• 
Consultant and subconsultant have not identified time within their level of effort to support 
public meetings.  Consultant and subconsultants will not participate in public meetings.  
Requests to support these activities will be part of an additional services request. 
• 
Weekly progress meetings are already included in the Phase 2 scope, but not included in the last 
year of UFES construction.   
• 
One Subconsultant currently identified: 
o ENGEO for geotechnical monitoring services 
TASK 7 – CONSTRUCTION PHASE SERVICES 
Consultant will provide ESDC for the UFES construction elements.   
Task 7.1 –Pre-Construction Conference 
Consultant will attend the pre-construction conference, assumed to be at the construction manager’s 
site. 
Task 7.2 – Attend Construction Progress Meetings via Teleconference 
During the construction phase, one Consultant representative will call into the weekly construction 
meetings. Agenda and minutes for the meetings will be prepared by others. 
The City has requested that Consultant limit participation in weekly progress meetings to not more than 
65 calls over a duration of approximately 126 weeks. Consultant shall not attend these meetings in 
person.  Consultant assumes that maximum participation will be every other week unless requested by 
City.  Consultant will have only one participant at these teleconference meetings. 
Construction Manager will inform Consultant as early as possible regarding construction schedule 
interruptions or delays related to the UFES construction elements.  If the City requests involvement in 
more than 65 meetings, then an amendment is warranted. 
Task 7.3: Review Shop Drawing Submittals and Second Submittals 
Consultant will review shop drawing submittals (including re-submittals). Construction Manager will 
receive, log and send each shop drawing submittal to Consultant for review.  Construction Manager will 
review submittals for completeness prior to sending to Consultant.  Consultant will provide quality 
control for each review. Following review, Consultant will return one marked up submittal and a shop 
drawing review letter with comments via email.  An assumed rate of re-submittal is 50%.  If the total re-
submittal rate exceeds 50% an amendment may be required to complete the submittal reviews.  A list of 
509 submittals is attached at the end of the scope.  Consultant will not re-review any submittal initially 
marked as “Make Corrections Noted.”   Consultant has budgeted a maximum of 1,982 hours between 
consultant and subconsultant for this task.  If the number of hours for review are exceeded, City shall 
authorize additional services by amendment. 
Consultant will review vendor operation and maintenance (O&M) documentation and associated 
equipment and appurtenances. This task also includes a review of resubmittals of 50% of the O&M 
documentation.  Consultant has not budgeted a separate line item for O&M manual review.   
53 of 328

--- page 54 ---
Page 4 of 22 
 
 
Consultant will review warranty documents assumed for architecture, electrical, instrumentation and 
controls, mechanical and landscape architecture.   
Task 7.8: Respond to Request for Information/Request for Clarification 
Consultant will review contractor Requests for Information (RFIs) and Requests for Clarification (RFCs). 
Each contractor RFI/RFC will be logged, processed and routed to the appropriate individual(s) to respond 
to the question. 120 RFIs/RFCs (total combined) are assumed.  Consultant has budgeted a maximum of 
665 hours between consultant and subconsultant for this task.  If the number of hours are exceeded, 
City shall authorize additional services by amendment 
Task 7.9: Attend Factory Witness Test 
Consultant will attend factory witness tests for the new pumps and the PLCs.  If the City desires, factory 
witness may be redefined as long as the number of witness events is not more than two. 
Task 7.10: Conduct/Attend Equipment and Material Conference  
Consultant will hold one material conference with the Contractor to discuss structural project elements, 
such as concrete mix design, and will prepare meeting minutes. 
Task 7.11: Conduct Field Visit 
The Engineer of Record is responsible in construction to establish the type and frequency of field 
reviews appropriate for the project and provide those services.  The City has required that the 
consultant limit field visits to sixteen site visits. These visits are assumed by consultant.  Subconsultant 
visits will be in Task 8. At the conclusion of the visit, the Consultant will prepare a brief trip report. 
Where field visits are required and consultant is not able to attend due to the City’s budgetary 
constraint, the City shall assume the responsibility for those reviews.  The consultant shall not be 
responsible, when performed by others, for observations of the quality of the installation nor for an 
evaluation of conformance to the design intent.  
Requests by CM or the contractor for others to attend site will require additional authorization.  City 
requests or requirements for additional site visits beyond the 16 identified will be authorized as part of 
additional services. 
Task 7.12: Prepare Change Orders 
Consultant will provide input to the Construction Manager for up to 12 change orders, which may 
contain multiple items.  The UFES project may involve construction changes to the design to 
accommodate field conditions.  
Task 7.13: Prepare Record Drawings  
Consultant will prepare Record Drawings based on the contractor’s “redline” marked-up drawings, 
provided that such markups are provided by the contractor within 2 months of the end of the 
construction period. The mark-ups are expected to contain clarifications, approved field modifications, 
change order work, and other significant construction revisions.  Consultant has budgeted a maximum 
of 300 hours for this task.  Consultant will limit record drawing updates to this amount of time. If 
desired, City shall authorize additional services by amendment for additional changes. Consultant will 
54 of 328

--- page 55 ---
Page 5 of 22 
 
 
not be responsible for verifying the validity of the red-line set provided by the contractor.  Consultant 
will not perform any field investigation to confirm final constructed facilities or resolve discrepancies. 
Files delivered by the consultant are assumed to be provided in PDF, native design files (Revit and Civil 
3D), and GIS.  No conversion to AutoCAD from the 3D models is assumed.  No changes will be made to 
the conformed specifications.  Once the initial submittals are provided to the City, if a request for 
changes results in more hours than budgeted an amendment will be warranted. 
Task 7.14: Support Startup and Commissioning 
Consultant will assist with startup and testing of the UFES.  Consultant has 56 hours budgeted for this 
task.  If the number of hours requested exceeds this budget, City shall authorize additional services by 
amendment. 
Task 7 Assumptions: 
The total construction time is estimated at 126 weeks.  Consultant will provide support during this time 
as directed by the City.  A level of effort is assumed for each activity.  Consultant budgets may shift 
between the subtasks.  If the number of hours requested by the City or their representative exceeds the 
budget, City shall authorize additional services by amendment. 
Construction Manager will be responsible for overall construction management, will schedule meetings 
and will prepare and distribute meeting notes for those meetings. 
Consultant has no control over Contractor and relies on Construction Manager to pre-review submittals 
to the Consultant for completeness. 
Construction Manager will coordinate and guide assignment of relevant submittals, RFIs, clarifications, 
change orders, test reports, etc.   Construction manager shall not direct changes to the contract via 
email communications.  All changes shall be formally acknowledged by City. 
Consultant shall be provided sufficient clarity of direction on individual submittals such that review time 
will not be impeded by multiple communications.  Each subsequent direction will constitute a new 
submittal review cycle.  All review comments shall come through the CM within the review process.  No 
communications via email outside of this submittal review process will be accepted. 
City reviews of submittals shall be conducted simultaneously with consultant reviews.  Comments on 
submittals that result in redesigns shall be escalated to the City for change request approval.  
Construction Manager will compile and provide the City a complete set of RFIs, submittals, change 
orders, and other construction-related correspondence at the completion of the construction project. 
Consultant will coordinate record drawing preparation at the completion of the project including 
providing Subconsultant with the red-line set and the desired final format of the record drawings. 
Consultant will not prepare an Operations and Maintenance manual for the project, nor will they review 
material prepared by others, unless specifically requested via a change request. 
Task 7 Deliverables: 
All deliverables are anticipated to be provided electronically, except for the paper copies required for 
agencies/utilities/permitting authorities.

• 
Submittal (all types) Reviews (pdf files)

The Consultant, City and Construction Manager will utilize Procore to review and process submittals and

TASK 8 GROUNDWATER & SETTLEMENT MONITORING SERVICES DURING CONSTRUCTION 
Construction phase monitoring is assumed to provide data to the city on a routine basis.  Reports will be 
provided electronically once the data is reviewed.  City is assumed to post the data on their website so 
that the public may view it.  
Task 8.1:  Construction Groundwater Monitoring 
This scope includes continued monitoring of the existing vibrating wire piezometers (VWPs) that were 
installed for the UFES and Conveyance packages during the design phase. The original scope included 
monitoring for 2 years. Consultant has continued to monitor the VWPs installed past the originally 
assumed 2 years. This item includes budget for the future monitoring around UFES and deeper 
excavations along Conveyance pipelines. 
• 
UFES Construction Monitoring VWPs:  Daily for 1st week, then weekly for 1 month, then 
monthly for 2 years (2 years total of monitoring, 5 total VWPs) 
• 
Existing Conveyance Pipelines: 2 days/quarter (involves field work, reviewing data and preparing 
a report) for 1 year of monitoring (1 year total of monitoring, up to 17 total VWPs) 
Deliverables:  Groundwater Monitoring Reports 
• 
UFES Construction Groundwater Memo VWPs:  Weekly for first 5 weeks, then monthly 
afterwards for 2 years total. 
• 
Groundwater Condition Evaluation Report for Existing Conveyance pipelines:  Every quarter for 
1 year total. 
Task 8.2 - Tieback & Shoring Observation 
Tieback and shoring observations include confirming shoring installation depths, tieback size, lengths 
and drilled angle as well as tieback tensioning and creep rate.  These observations will provide close 
monitoring and feedback to prevent/correct excessive shoring deflection.  Contractor or Design-Build 
Subcontractor will perform all observation during shoring and tie-back installation. Therefore, the 
registered professional retained by the Contractor will sign off on the Building Department Condition of 
Approval (COA). Consultant will provide responses to questions related to soil conditions encountered, if 
requested. 
• 
RFI and as-needed consultation during shoring and tie-back installation 
Deliverables: 
Responses to requests for information. 
56 of 328

--- page 57 ---
Page 7 of 22 
 
 
Task 8.3 - Micropile Observation 
As Geotechnical Engineer of Record (GEOR), Consultant is required to be onsite full-time during critical 
construction elements such as foundation construction. Micropiles are considered part of the 
foundation system, therefore observation from the GEOR will be needed. Consultant will sign off as 
GEOR for the micropile foundation system. 
• 
Geotechnical observation during installation of production micropiles: Assume up to 20 days of 
full-time observation during micropile installation. Include field observation, data review and 
preparation of progress reports. 
• 
Review of production micropile installation logs: Assume most of the production piles will not be 
observed by Consultant. These piles will be observed by the construction manager or a 
representative of the contractor. The construction manager or their representative will prepare 
daily installation logs and provide them to Consultant for review within 24 hours. Consultant will 
continue to serve as the GEOR; however, the Consultant cannot be liable for errors and 
omissions of the installation logs prepared by the construction manager, contractor or the City’s 
3rd party representative. In addition, Consultant cannot be liable for construction delays 
associated with late submittal of the installation logs for review. 
• 
Geotechnical observation during test micropile installation and load testing: Assume up to 10 
test piles will be installed in 1 day and up to 2 days of testing. Consultant will provide up to 3 
days of full-time observation. 
Deliverables: 
Review micropile load test results and prepare approval letter. 
Production Micropile observation summary letters for UFES (Assume 2 letters) 
Task 8.4 - Testing and Observation During Construction 
As the GEOR, Consultant is required to observe and review the geotechnical aspects of the construction 
activities to confirm recommendations are being followed. A 3rd party agency will perform soil testing 
and observations during fill placement.  Daily reports and inspections prepared by the selected 3rd party 
testing agency will be provided to the Consultant for review and approval within 36 hours. The 
Consultant will continue to serve as the GEOR; however, the Consultant cannot be liable for missed 
inspections or errors and omissions arising from the services of the 3rd party testing agency. 
• 
Improvements:  Review tests taken during soil backfill activities 
• 
Foundation Construction - Review of test results during subgrade preparation and onsite visits 
prior to concrete pour: Consultant will perform foundation subgrade observation at electrical 
building and UFES excavation. Consultant will provide approval prior to concrete pour when 
subgrade is deemed competent.  Assume up to 5 site visits and 20 hours of consultation. 
• 
Pavement Construction - Review of tests taken of subgrade preparation, and aggregate base and 
HMA placement: Assume up to 3 site visits to observe proof rolling and provide field 
recommendation if unstable subgrade condition is encountered. 
Deliverables:

Summary letters and final reporting, up to 3 final reports (soil backfill and placement; foundation 
subgrade approval; pavement construction).

CITY OF SAN MATEO
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Agenda Report
City Hall
330 W. 20th Avenue
San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  4
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
File ID: 20-3007
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Drew Corbett, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
May 18, 2020 
SUBJECT:
Community Development Block Grant 2020-21 Annual Action Plan – Adoption; and Community Participation Plan and 
2018-2022 Consolidated Plan – Amendments 
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt the 2020-21 Annual Action Plan for the Community Development Block Grant and HOME programs, and adopt 
amendments to the Community Participation Plan and the 2018-22 Consolidated Plan.
BACKGROUND:
The Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) Program provides flexible funding for community development projects 
and programs to assist individuals and families from extremely low- to moderate-income households as defined by the 
Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD). San Mateo receives an entitlement grant based on a national 
formula and has participated in this program since 1977. 
The City also received an entitlement amount of HOME funds from 1994 to 2015 that was used to assist housing programs 
and projects for very low-income households. In 2016, the City joined a consortium with the County of San Mateo and 
South San Francisco to pool our HOME funds to provide more efficiency and timeliness in expending those funds. The City 
still collects loan payments from loans made prior to 2015 and must re- program those funds into HOME-eligible projects. 
The application process for these federal programs includes the adoption of a 3-5 year strategy called the Consolidated 
Plan (Con Plan), and the submission of an Annual Action Plan each year for specific budgeting and programming of federal 
funds and other local resources for housing and community development activities. The public process for review and 
comment of these plans is incorporated into the Community Participation Plan (CPP).
In March 2020, the Coronavirus Aid, Relief, and Economic Security (CARES) Act was passed that will provide additional 
funding to the City of San Mateo through the CDBG program to specifically address the COVID pandemic. In order to 
expedite getting these funds out into the community, HUD has approved some program waivers that require slight 
modifications to our Annual Plan this year. 
2020-21 Annual Action Plan 
The Annual Action Plan outlines the City’s budget for the coming program year with details of the programs and projects 
that will be undertaken to address the needs identified in the Consolidated Plan. The CDBG grant is $747,853 for the 2020-
21 program year and the CDBG-CV funding from the CARES program is $439,938. The remaining funds for the budget will 
come from program income and prior year resources. The major activities are: 
• Administration – a maximum of 20% of the CDBG grant is eligible for administrative costs. The fair housing grant of 
$25,000 is included in the administration budget.
76 of 328

--- page 77 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
 • Community Funding – the cap for public services is 15% of the grant and prior year program income. The Community 
Resources Commission identified non-profit agencies for provision of public services to meet priority needs at its meeting 
on February 20, 2020. This year, HUD has granted a waiver of the 15% public service cap if the funds are used for COVID 
related services. The City Council provided staff direction to use the $440,000 in CARES funds to Samaritan House for 
emergency rent assistance, $120,000 of which will be reserved for family childcare providers that rent their homes. Staff 
also recommends additional $60,000 to Samaritan House to provide the staffing support they need for the emergency rent 
program, as well as other supportive services due to the pandemic. 
• Minor Home Repair – the City will fund three providers for home repair, energy upgrades, and accessibility modifications 
to eligible households.
 • Public Facilities - provides funds for capital improvements to buildings owned by nonprofit agencies. This can be also be 
used for tenant improvements required for a new location for the Worker Resource Center. 
• Street Improvement Project – the Department of Public Works will manage this project, prioritizing public safety 
improvements to streets and sidewalks located in the CDBG Priority Target Area consisting of the North Shoreview and 
North Central neighborhoods. 
• Reserve - staff is recommending that about $220,000 that would normally be budged for street improvements remain in 
reserve until more information about community needs related to COVID-19 is determined later in the program year. This 
allows some flexibility given the uncertainty as to the extent of future community impacts.
 • HOME Funds – an estimated $642,000 will be available to support the affordable housing project at the City’s 
Downtown Opportunity Sites, which is currently going through the planning entitlement process for 225 rental units, set 
for approval in summer of 2020. This will be combined with other City affordable housing funds for a total of $7.5 million 
in financial assistance for the housing portion of the project. 
Citizen Participation Plan 
Typically, the CPP requires a 30-day public comment period to adopt or amend the Consolidated Plan or the Annual Plan, 
and a 15-day comment period to revise the CPP itself. Through the CARES Act, HUD has reduced the public comment 
period to 5 days for Con Plan and CPP amendments. The 30-day comment period for the Annual Plan remains in place. 
Also given the current shelter in place orders, in-person public hearings are not feasible. The amendments to the CPP 
provide for shorter comment periods no less than five days due to emergency situations, and allow for virtual meetings, as 
long as there is a method to provide for "real time" comments, when gathering in person is not allowed.
Consolidated Plan 
The CPP provides that the Consolidated Plan requires a Substantial Amendment if a new project or activity is added to the 
original plan, or if the funding amount for a project or activity changes by 50% or more. The Con Plan did not anticipate 
collecting significant HOME loan repayments, so they were not programmed at the time it was adopted. The Substantial 
Amendment adds the HOME funds for the affordable housing project to the Con Plan. The initial Con Plan also budgeted a 
total of $500,000 for Community Funding program for 5 years, so the additional $439,938 in CARES funding increases that 
program significantly and is included in the amendment

Executive Summary 
AP-05 Executive Summary - 91.200(c), 91.220(b)
1.
Introduction
The Annual Action Plan (Annual Plan) is required of the City of San Mateo by the U.S. Department of 
Housing and Urban Development (HUD) in order for the City to receive federal Community Development 
Block Grant (CDBG) funds. The City's Annual Plan for fiscal year 2020-21 is the third year of the multi-
year 2018-22 Consolidated Plan. The Annual Plan outlines needs and develops strategies to address 
priority needs of low- and moderate-income populations in San Mateo. This fiscal year is unique in its 
strategies due to the emergence of the COVID-19 pandemic. The city has had a new source of CDBG 
funding but also an influx of new challenges that have risen directly from the effects of the virus. 
Additional public outreach meetings have been held and additional programs have been funded to aptly 
respond to these new emerging concerns.
2.
Summarize the objectives and outcomes identified in the Plan  
This could be a restatement of items or a table listed elsewhere in the plan or a reference to 
another location. It may also contain any essential items from the housing and homeless needs 
assessment, the housing market analysis or the strategic plan.
The City's Consolidated Plan identifies the following needs and has developed goals and activities that 
further HUD's program goals. 
Need: Affordable Housing
Goal: Increase, maintain, and improve the supply of affordable housing for low- and moderate-income 
families and individuals. 
Activities: The City will use CDBG and local funds for development of housing, acquisition and/or 
rehabilitation of housing, minor home repairs, weatherization, and accessibility modifications. 
Additionally, the City will continue to administer its existing below-market rate housing rental and 
ownership units. 
Need: Public Facilities Improvements
Goal: Preserve and improve public facilities that serve a high percentage of low- and moderate-income 
families as well as those with special needs. 
Activities: The City will use CDBG funds, when feasible, to make accessibility modification to public 
facilities and to provide funds for rehabilitation of facilities with urgent needs. 
80 of 328

--- page 81 ---
Draft Annual Action Plan
2020
2
OMB Control No: 2506-0117 (exp. 06/30/2018)
Need: Public Services
Goal: Provide services to improve quality of life for low- and moderate-income families and individuals, 
including those at risk of becoming homeless and special needs populations.
Activities: The City will allocated the 15% of its entitlement and 15% of the previous year's program 
income, as allowed by CDBG regulation, for the Community Funding Program. These funds will be 
granted to non-profit agencies for provision of public services. 
Need: Community Development
Goal: Infrastructure improvements in the CDBG Priority Neighborhood.
Activities: The City will use CDBG funds for capital projects such as replacement of failed streets and 
sidewalks, accessible curb ramps, traffic calming, as well as pedestrian and bikeways improvements. The 
Department of Public Works will manage projects. 
Need: Affirmatively Further Fair Housing
Goal: Address fair housing issues and contributing factors as determined by the Assessment of Fair 
Housing, which was approved by HUD in January 2018.
Activities: The City will allocate funds from administration for provision of fair housing services to be 
granted to a non-profit partner. The City will also work towards the goals from the Assessment of Fair 
Housing . 
3.
Evaluation of past performance 
This is an evaluation of past performance that helped lead the grantee to choose its goals or 
projects.
The City recognizes the ongoing needs of the San Mateo community and continues to fund core service 
needs. All of the Community Funding programs have met or exceeded their goals for service, showing an 
ongoing need for the services they are providing the community. The cost of housing continues to be 
extremely high in San Mateo and as a result many of the activities focus on services related to housing.
The City's Minor Home Repair programs have been slower to meet their goals, but all three 
organizations and City staff agree that there is a great need for their services. During the past year, City 
staff met with agency staff to discuss challenges in providing these services. As a result of those 
meetings, the City adjusted grant amounts to accurately reflect average project costs and realistic 
project goals. The City will again update goals and grant amounts for the 2020-21 Program Year, and re-
evaluate grantees at the end of the year.

One concern from the sub grantees is that clients may need more repairs than can be funded within the 
scope of repair.  To that end a Housing Rehabilitation Loan program is being reinstated with repaid 
CalHOME loan funds to address this need.
For the 2020-21 fiscal year the City will continue to allocate $400,000 for Street and Sidewalk 
Reconstruction activities . Each year funding is provided for repairs that improve the pedestrian, bike 
and auto safety in the CDBG priority neighborhood. Based on input from both community members and 
Public Works department, there is demonstrated ongoing need for this type of funding.

well as the goals set forth in the 2018-22 Consolidated Plan.

AP-10 Consultation - 91.100, 91.200(b), 91.215(l)
1.
Introduction
The City consulted with many different stakeholders in developing this Annual Action Plan. Meetings 
were held internally with the Department of Public Works regarding prioritizing street reconstruction 
and pedestrian safety projects. Non-profit partners from the area were invited to Community Needs 
Assessment workshops and Community Relations Commission meetings. 
Provide a concise summary of the jurisdiction’s activities to enhance coordination between 
public and assisted housing providers and private and governmental health, mental health 
and service agencies (91.215(l)).
Throughout the Annual Action Plan period, the City will maintain its relationships with organizations that 
serve the public, especially low- and moderate-income residents. Efforts will include:

Working with other entitlement jurisdictions in San Mateo County to coordinate and streamline 
the CDBG process

Working with non-profit social service providers, the County of San Mateo, other entitlement 
jurisdictions, and other stakeholders to coordinate the provision of needed services in the 
community

Providing funds through the community funding program to non-profit service providers 

Working with non-profit organizations, private developers, and the County of San Mateo to 
build and maintain affordable housing

Working with the Continuum of Care, Homeless Outreach Team, and non-profit service 
providers to coordinate homeless services
Describe coordination with the Continuum of Care and efforts to address the needs of 
homeless persons (particularly chronically homeless individuals and families, families with 
children, veterans, and unaccompanied youth) and persons at risk of homelessness.
The Continuum of Care (COC) guides the implementation of the county's housing and service system to 
meet the needs of homeless individuals and families. The City of San Mateo participates in COC 
meetings and monitors decision-making to better understand latest trends in homeless outreach. The 
COC coordinates the following activities:

System planning (identifying gaps, developing strategies to fill gaps, responding to emerging 
best practices, etc.)

Setting funding priorities for Emergency Solutions Grant and COC funds

Assessing system performance and making system redesigns as needed

Coordinating with other planning entities such as the Community Action Agency
84 of 328

--- page 85 ---
Draft Annual Action Plan
2020
6
OMB Control No: 2506-0117 (exp. 06/30/2018)

Undertakes a wide range of efforts to meet the needs of homeless individuals and famillies
Chronically Homeless: COC has created a multi-disciplinary, bilingual, Homeless Outreach Team (HOT) to 
conduct intensive outreach and engagement with unsheltered and chronically homeless individuals and 
families located throughout the County, with specialized HOT teams in the cities of San Mateo, Redwood 
City, South San Francisco, Half Moon Bay, Pacifica, and East Palo Alto.
Families with children: To reduce the number of unsheltered families, the COC has developed a rapid re-
housing program. The San Mateo County Human Services Agency has provided funding for a motel 
voucher program to assist families with children that are waiting to access shelter.
Veterans: Needs include housing and assistance for homeless, employment and education services, and 
improved and increased liaisons with the Veterans Benefits Administration. 
Youth: Currently, HUD COC funds are provided to the San Mateo County Mental Health Association to 
operate its Support and Advocacy for Young Adults in Transition Program, which provides case 
management and housing search/stabilization services to homeless youth. The San Mateo County 
Housing Authority administers the Family Unification Program vouchers. 
Describe consultation with the Continuum(s) of Care that serves the jurisdiction’s area in 
determining how to allocate ESG funds, develop performance standards for and evaluate 
outcomes of projects and activities assisted by ESG funds, and develop funding, policies and 
procedures for the operation and administration of HMIS
The City of San Mateo does not receive Emergency Solutions Grant (ESG) funding, as the San Mateo 
County Department of Housing (DOH) is the sole recipient in the county. However, the City does 
participate in COC meetings as part of its ongoing responsibility in receiving HUD funding. DOH 
coordinates closely with the COC in regards to the County's ESG, COC, and CDBG funding and is 
represented on the COC Steering Committee. DOH has also delegated responsibility for management of 
all ESG funds, plush the portion of the County CDBG funds used for homeless activities, to the COC Lead 
Agency, and the San Mateo County Human Services Agency (HSA). Management responsibilities include 
issuing requests for proposals for ESG funding, awarding contracts, gathering community input, data 
analysis, and contract monitoring. The COC Lead Agency is also the Homeless Management Information 
System (HMIS) Lead Agency and develops the policies and procedures for operation and administration 
of HMIS for ESG funded projects.

Expected Resources
AP-15 Expected Resources - 91.420(b), 91.220(c)(1,2)
Introduction
Anticipated resources from CDBG include the 2020 entitlement grant of $747,853 plus $439,938 from the CARES Act to be used specifically to 
prevent the spread of coronavirus 19 (COVID-19) and facilitate assistance to eligible communities, households, and persons economically 
impacted by COVID-19.  It is possible that additional funds in an unknown amount will be allocated to San Mateo later.  Additional funds will be 
used for the same purposes.
Further, eligible CDBG expenses incurred as of March 27, 2020, which is the date in which President Trump signed the CARES Act, and paid for 
with nonfederal funds may be repaid with CDBG, including those made under the CARES Act. These pre-award costs will meet all HUD 
requirements applicable to CDBG including those under the CARES Act.  Unless waived by HUD, CDBG pre-award costs for FY 2020-2021 will not 
exceed 25% of the grant and will be used for the CDBG eligible activities as indicated above.

Annual Action Plan
2019
19
OMB Control No: 2506-0117 (exp. 06/30/2018)
The City receives direct entitlement funds from Federal CDBG Program that are used to address identified needs. The City is also part of the San 
Mateo County HOME Consortium; HOME funds formerly granted directly to the City are now combined with the County of San Mateo and the 
City of South San Francisco in order to use the funds more efficiently. The City also receives HOME loan repayments from projects assisted with 
HOME funds provided prior to joining the consortium in 2015.
The City manages a varied portfolio of housing loans from several programs including Housing Rehabilitation and First Time Homebuyer 
programs as well as developer loans for new construction or acquisition/rehabilitation projects. Program income from this portfolio augments 
the CDBG and HOME funds as well as now defunct programs such as Redevelopment and former CalHOME owner rehab loan program. Loan 
repayments from loans funded with former Redevelopment funds are deposited in the Low Mod Housing Asset Fund to be used for future 
affordable housing programs.  The City also sets aside the equivalent of 20% of the property tax increment attributed to the former 
Redevelopment areas for housing, known as “boomerang funds”. The City collects subordination processing fees and fractional unit fees 
associated with its Below Market Rate Program in its City Housing Fund, which is typically used to assist regional housing initiatives that are 
outside of the San Mateo’s city limits. 
. The City Council adopted a commercial linkage fee ordinance which became effective on 11/5/16. New commercial projects with square 
footage in excess of 5,000 square feet pay a fee to mitigate the impact of new jobs on local housing supply.
Starting this year, the City will receive and annual allocation of the State Permanent Local Housing Allocation (PHLA) as provided by  the Building 
Homes and Jobs Act to increase the supply of affordable housing.  It is estimated that the City will receive approximately $340,000 for 2020.  
There are a number of new State programs that City will watch and apply for as they become available including Local Early Action Planning 
grants to support planning efforts to increase the supply of housing, as well as the Local Housing Trust Fund Program.  The City also tracks and 
supports legislation that promotes and increases resources for affordable housing.
Section 8 funds are provided to San Mateo residents through the San Mateo County Housing Authority. McKinney-Vento Homeless Assistance 
Act funds are managed by the San Mateo County Human Services Agency as part of the Continuum of Care, in which San Mateo participates. The 
County of San Mateo also supports housing projects countywide with its HOME and CDBG funds which often are used to leverage City resources. 
The Housing Endowment and Regional Trust (HEART) of San Mateo County is a public/private partnership whose goal is to raise funds to create 
affordable housing opportunities in San Mateo County. 
Low-Income Housing Tax Credits are offered through the State on a competitive process and with the dissolution of Redevelopment, 
98 of 328

--- page 99 ---
Annual Action Plan
2019
20
OMB Control No: 2506-0117 (exp. 06/30/2018)
applications for these funds are expected to become even more in demand and competitive. The State also has also set aside a portion of the 
Cap and Trade funds for housing located close to transit in its Affordable Housing Sustainable Communities program. The City will support 
developer applications for tax credits and other State Housing programs as they become available for appropriate and eligible projects. 
If appropriate, describe publically owned land or property located within the jurisdiction that may be used to address the needs 
identified in the plan
The City received a one acre site to be used for affordable housing as part of the development agreement executed for Bay Meadows II Master 
Plan.  The City choose BRIDGE Housing as the nonprofit development partner, who is moving forward with the predevelopment process. The City 
and BRIDGE are taking advantage of the State Density Bonus Law and are planning for 68 affordable rental housing units on the site. The project 
received it's tax credit allocation in 2018 and began construction in March 2019. 
As a result of the dissolution of the Redevelopment Agency of the City of San Mateo, a Long Range Property Management Plan has been drafted 
and approved by the State. City chose MidPen Housing for the development of two sites (approx. 2.4 acres total) located in downtown San 
Mateo that were owned by the former Redevelopment Agency. The sites will be developed with 225 affordable housing units and a public 
parking garage.. The project is is expected to obtain full planning approvals and an executed Disposition, Development and Loan Agreement  in 
summer of 2020 and construction to begin by the end of 2021.

Annual Action Plan
2019
OMB Control No: 2506-0117 (exp. 06/30/2018)
AP-35 Projects - 91.420, 91.220(d)
Introduction 
Activities planned for 2020-21 are similar to those from recent years. The City will continue to use CDBG 
administration funds for provision of fair housing activities, public services for grants to non-profit public 
service agencies, and the remainder of CDBG funds for minor home repair programs, community 
development projects, and economic development.  
This year the additional CARES funds will be used  for eligible CDBG activities including, but not limited 
to, assisting low- and moderate-income households with rental assistance for no more than three 
months, grab and go/delivery meal programs, support to microenterprise businesses,  and support of 
other COVID-19 response services.    The City will also utilize the HUD waiver of the 15% public service 
cap in order to provide additional funding for COVID -19 related services.
#
Project Name
1
Community Funding Program
2
Home Energy and Repair Program
3
CDBG Admin
4
Street and Sidewalk Reconstruction
Table 7 – Project Information
Describe the reasons for allocation priorities and any obstacles to addressing underserved 
needs
The housing, social service, and community development needs of the community are overwhelming 
when compared to funding available from CDBG and other sources. Allocations of funding are made 
with careful consideration of the community's needs and input from the citizen participation process 
and the Community Relations Commission. City staff, along with other jurisdictions and community 
partners, cooperate in order to streamline processes and avoid duplication of services in an effort to 
maximize the available resources.
This year additional funding is provided for the Community Funding program to address the urgent 
needs of community members impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic.  The City has left approximately 
$221,000 unprogrammed to be allocated later after the first quarter of the fiscal year. Program feedback 
from service providers will be used to determine which needs require additional funding.

The City of San Mateo provides a number of programs that assist low-income individuals and 
households based and therefore may be located anywhere within the city limits of San Mateo.  In 
addition, the City has identified a CDBG Priority Neighborhood by utilizing the low-income definitions 
provided by HUD.  This area includes any census tract or block group with at least 50% of the persons

AP-75 Barriers to affordable housing -91.420, 91.220(j)
Introduction
The City is committed to using available tools to increase the availability of affordable housing. Current programs include an inclusionary zoning 
ordinance, commercial linkage fee, and the City also works with developers of 100% affordable projects using local funding and land. 
Actions it planned to remove or ameliorate the negative effects of public policies that serve as barriers to affordable housing such 
as land use controls, tax policies affecting land, zoning ordinances, building codes, fees and charges, growth limitations, and 
policies affecting the return on residential investment
Streamlining the approval process for residential developments is a high priority for the City of San Mateo.  A number of efforts are planned this 
program year.

Consistent with 2016 state housing legislation, the City Council adopted a new Accessory Dwelling Unit ordinance in March 2017, which 
allows for one Accessory Dwelling Unit (aka secondary units) as of right within residential zoning districts. The ordinance includes ADU 
size limitation, parking exemptions and requirements, location requirements, and other standards. Although the number of applications 
has increased with these changes, the City continues to look into streamlining the process and will propose  additional  adjustments to 
the ordinance in Fall 2020 .

The City formed an in-house team to look at streamlining the development review process and will also hire a consultant during this 
program year to assist in redesigned the current processes.

During this program year, the City will conduct a study to evaluate all development fees to measure the impacts on residential 
construction, and consider reduction in fees for affordable housing project

AP-85 Other Actions - 91.420, 91.220(k)
Introduction
Actions planned to address obstacles to meeting underserved needs
The recent booming economy has placed further stress on low wage earning families and the cost of 
housing. The City will use its limited resources to address these needs in accordance with the priorities 
identified by the Community Resources Commission.  Federal funding sources are unpredictable, so the 
City has made financial adjustments and will focus on opportunities to strengthen and/or support the 
businesses of San Mateo that are the providers of jobs, income and security to its residents.  The City 
continues to look for new ways to streamline procedures and collaborate with other community groups 
and has especially focused on volunteerism.  With the CDBG Public Services grants, the City will continue 
to partner with its nonprofit business and service providers to provide direct support and basic needs 
services (food, shelter, clothing, etc.) for residents most in need. The CRC also has prioritized job 
training/small business support, as well as capital improvements in the CDBG Priority Areas.
Through the Community Resources Commission the remarks received at the community needs 
workshops and hearings were reviewed and summarized in the Citizen Participation section of this 
document. Each year the Community Funding grants are selected as a tool to address the underserved 
needs of the community. The primary obstacle in addressing most community needs is available 
funding.  The Commission has tried to allocate its limited funds in a manner that provides unduplicated 
services and tries to stretch the funding to be cost effective. 
Actions planned to foster and maintain affordable housing
The City works collaboratively with numerous non profit organizations and other jurisdictions in 
the preservation and development of affordable housing.  The County of San Mateo and all of the cities 
and towns in the county formed a workgroup called 21 Elements, which was formed to collaborate and 
share best practices on housing policies and programs for the adoption of the Housing Elements in the 
respective General Plans.  This group has continued to meet quarterly to share information and share in 
costs of studies, such as the countywide Nexus Study in order to establish Affordable Housing and 
Commercial Linkage Fees. Through this workgroup the City of San Mateo adopted a Commercial Linkage 
Fee in 2016.  This fee is charged to new commercial developments to help mitigate the impact on 
housing demand created by increasing jobs in the community.
The City also has local funding sources that can support the preservation and development of affordable 
housing besides HUD resources.  The City has continued to pledge "Boomerang" funds for housing from 
its general fund.  This is a portion of property taxes that were previously set aside for housing in the 
former Redevelopment Areas.  The City also still collects loan repayments from loans made by the 
122 of 328

--- page 123 ---
Annual Action Plan
2019
OMB Control No: 2506-0117 (exp. 06/30/2018)
former Redevelopment Agency that are re-used for affordable housing. All of the City's local funds are 
targeted to assist acquisition, rehab or new construction of affordable housing.
New housing opportunities include the development of one acre site at Bay Meadows which was 
provided by the developer as part of a development agreement with the City. Construction of 68 family 
units utilizing Tax Credits plus local funds pledged by the County and City. The project began 
construction in March 2019. The City will also entered into a development agreement for two former 
Redevelopment Agency sites downtown that will include 164 units targeted to mixed incomes.  The 
details of the affordability levels, the funding assistance and other public benefit will be negotiated 
during the 2020-21 program year.
The City continues implement its inclusionary Below Market Rate Program that requires developers of 
new market rate housing to setaside 15% of the units to be affordable. These units account for 25% of 
all the affordable housing units in the City.  There continues to be developer interest in utilizing the 
State Density Bonus program that expands on the City's program and can potentially provide either 
more or deeper affordability in private developments. 
The City updated its Accessory Dwelling Unit program in 2018 and is working with the County and 21 
Elements to market and encourage the production of small units incorporated into single family 
properties citywide. The City will adopt further revisions to the program in 2020.
The City also relies on other adopted plans to guide housing production and policies including its 
General Plan, including the Housing Element, the 2016 Housing Task Force report, and various specific 
plans such as Rail Corridor and Downtown Specific Plans.
The City has funds that have been repaid over time from loans made through the State Dept. of Housing 
and Community Development's CalHome program. These funds will be made available for a Housing 
Rehabilitation Loan Program available to low-income homeowners in the City. 
Actions planned to reduce lead-based paint hazards
The City will continue to use its adopted procedures and guidelines to evaluate and reduce lead-based 
paint hazards as required for each eligible project performed using CDBG and HOME funding. This will 
apply to assisted acquisition, rehabilitation, the Minor Home Repair and Paint programs, and/or 
rehabilitation projects including Rebuilding Together Peninsula.
Actions planned to reduce the number of poverty-level families
The actions to work toward eliminating poverty in San Mateo include:

Strengthen the economic base in order to create and retain job opportunities in San Mateo:

Provide affordable housing: Complete development of 68 units on the Bay Meadows one acre

site and continue assisting with the entitlement process on 164 units of housing on two 
Downtown parcels.

Provide social services to help people reach self-sufficiency through public services grants.
Actions planned to develop institutional structure 
Gaps previously identified in institutional structure included reduction in staffing due to severe budget 
reductions, limiting institutional capacity. This will continue to be a reality for San Mateo and other 
jurisdictions and non profit agencies as well.  This requires more careful coordination in services and as 
well as administration of programs.  The Countywide CDBG Cohort group is an example of how staff 
from several cities coordinates public service agreements and monitoring in order to streamline the 
process. During the upcoming year the group will continue to share best practices and identify program 
areas that can be streamlined.
Actions planned to enhance coordination between public and private housing and social 
service agencies
The City will continue to collaborate with public and private housing developers as it manages its 
ongoing BMR program and manages new subsidized housing projects.  In City sponsored affordable 
housing projects, it is expected that services are provided to the occupants such as transportation 
subsidy and information, after school programs, social activities, information and referral to other 
services including health, credit and food and clothing.  The community is fortunate that these agencies 
are very well connected already, and the City assists when it can to strengthen the networks.
